# Story 0000055 – Users can queue ingest and re-embed requests

## Implementation Plan

This is a list of steps that must be followed whilst working on a story. The first step of any plan is to copy this file to a new markdown document that starts with an index padded with zeroes starting at 1 and the title of the story. eg: ./planning/0000001-initial-skeleton-setup.md
Create (or reuse if it already exists) the feature branch for this phase using the established naming convention (for example `feature/<number>-<Title>`).
The Description, Acceptance Criteria & Out Of Scope sections must be fully documented to the point where a very junior, inexperienced developer who has never seen the product before would be able to read and understand what we want to do and why.
The Questions sections should be populated by an AI at the start of the planning phase, as soon as the initial description is provided. As these questions get answered, the questions should be removed and relevent information should be added to the other sections. The Questions section must be empty before creating tasks.

### Description

Users can currently start ingest and re-embed work only when the server is idle. If another ingest operation is already running, later requests are rejected as busy instead of being remembered and run in order. This is frustrating for both humans and AI automation because the user must retry later, and a server restart loses the intent to run that work entirely.

This story adds a durable whole-request queue for ingest and re-embed work. The queue is intentionally about request orchestration, not about how one ingest run chunks files or dispatches embeddings internally. When a request arrives, the server should normalize it to the canonical embed target path, store one queue record in MongoDB, and either start it immediately if nothing is active or leave it waiting until earlier queued work finishes.

Queue-aware success responses now need two identifiers with different jobs. `requestId` is the durable queue identifier for the queued request itself. `runId` remains the runtime ingest identifier once work has actually started. A waiting item can therefore return `requestId` without an active `runId` yet, while an immediately started or later-started item can expose both.

The queue should use one MongoDB collection for both waiting and currently running items. The currently running item stays in the collection until it reaches a terminal outcome. Once that run completes, the server must remove that queue record before it attempts to start the next oldest item. If that delete fails, the server should log an error, surface an error state in the frontend, and keep retrying the delete with backoff while the queue remains stalled. This ordering matters because a restart should be able to look at the same collection and simply start the oldest remaining item again without relying on a second persistent "in progress" state. The persisted queue-state model should stay deliberately small: `waiting` before a run starts, `running` while that queue item owns the active ingest, and `cleanup-blocked` when terminal work finished but the queue record could not yet be removed. There is no separate persisted `abandoned` state for this story; on startup, any leftover `running` record is treated as the abandoned previously-active item and retried.

This story also fixes duplicate-request behavior. If a request arrives for a canonical embed target path that is already waiting in the queue, the server should not insert a second queue item. Instead, it should update that existing waiting item's stored settings in place, keep the same queue request id and queue position, return success, and log that the queued work was intentionally updated rather than duplicated. Those in-place updates should preserve the original queue identity and ordering metadata, including the durable request id, the original `createdAt`, and the original source-surface provenance, while refreshing `updatedAt` and replacing the stored normalized request settings with the latest request. If the matching item is already running, the server should still avoid creating a second queue item, but it should not try to mutate the active run's settings mid-flight. This latest-settings-wins rule for waiting items applies across both start-ingest and re-embed requests once the server has resolved them to the same canonical embed target path.

MongoDB is required for this queue feature. If Mongo is unavailable, queueable ingest and re-embed requests should be rejected before they start. This story does not provide a degraded "run immediately without persistence" mode because that would break the durable queue contract and make restart behavior inconsistent.

Agent and workflow behavior must remain predictable. If a re-embed request is triggered from a flow, command JSON file, or MCP surface that currently waits for terminal completion, that caller should still wait until the queued request actually finishes. Queueing changes how long the caller may need to wait, but it does not change the contract from blocking completion to fire-and-forget. The preferred server behavior is event-driven waiting for the queue item and ingest run to reach a terminal state, not a short fixed timeout loop. A much longer safety timeout can still exist as a final guard for broken listeners or lost state, but it should not be the normal reason a correctly queued request fails. When Mongo-backed queue persistence is unavailable, REST should surface that as `503 Service Unavailable` with `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE`, while MCP, flows, and commands should preserve the same `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` meaning as structured retryable errors rather than flattening it into a generic invalid request.

The frontend must also make queued work visible. When a repository is queued for re-embed, the UI should show that it is queued and show its queue position so the user knows the request was accepted and is waiting its turn. That queue position should count only waiting work, so `1` means “next in line” rather than “behind the currently running item plus everything else.” The repository list is the required source of truth for this state; this story does not need a separate top-of-page queue card. In practice, queued state and queue position should be added to the shared repository-list payload so the existing repo-list mirrors stay aligned, while unrelated flow-facing or generic status payloads do not need their own separate queue-position fields. If a brand-new repository is queued before it has ever been ingested, the repository list should synthesize a temporary row right away so queued start-ingest work is visible there too. This should be a stable status in the ingest surfaces, not just a short-lived toast.

Queue acceptance also changes submission behavior on the ingest page. While another run is active, start-ingest and re-embed actions should still be submittable so they can join the durable queue, rather than remaining disabled just because work is already running. This story does not require new hidden client-side queue fields or a separate local queue cache; the browser should keep submitting the visible current values, and queued visibility should come back from the shared server-side repository-list contract.

The client-side state rules should stay simple. After a queueable submission is accepted, the form may keep its visible values locally for user convenience, but those retained values must not mutate an already accepted queue item unless the user explicitly submits again. Removing the active-run disable gate also does not unlock fields that are disabled for a different reason, such as the existing embedding-model lock.

The queue is FIFO by creation time. On server startup, if the queue collection contains leftover items and no ingest is already active, the server should first retry or resolve any cleanup-blocked queue item that previously failed deletion, and only then attempt to start the oldest remaining waiting item automatically. Because the active item remains in Mongo until terminal completion, this gives the queue at-least-once recovery semantics after restart without needing a second persistent run-state table.

### Acceptance Criteria

- Ingest and re-embed requests use one durable MongoDB queue collection rather than being rejected immediately whenever another ingest run is active.
- Every queueable request is normalized to the canonical embed target path before dedupe and queue insertion decisions are made.
- If MongoDB is unavailable, queueable ingest and re-embed requests are rejected before any new run starts.
- When MongoDB is unavailable, queueable ingest and re-embed requests return a clear retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` error rather than a generic server failure.
- The queue uses one collection for both waiting and currently running items; a running item remains in the collection until terminal completion.
- Queue documents persist one coarse queue-state enum with exactly `waiting`, `running`, and `cleanup-blocked`.
- If no ingest is active when a request is accepted, the server inserts the queue item and then starts that oldest queued item immediately.
- If an ingest is already active when a request is accepted, the server inserts the queue item and leaves it waiting in FIFO order.
- Queue order is FIFO by queue creation time.
- On server startup, if no ingest is active and the queue collection contains leftover items, the server attempts to start the oldest remaining item automatically.
- On startup, any leftover `running` queue item is treated as abandoned previously-active work to retry; this story does not require a separate persisted `abandoned` state.
- When an ingest or re-embed run reaches a terminal outcome, the server attempts to delete that queue item before it attempts to start the next queued item.
- If queue-item deletion fails after a terminal run, the server logs an error, shows an error state in the frontend, retries the delete with backoff, and does not start the next queued item until that queue-record removal problem is resolved.
- If a request arrives for a canonical embed target path that is already waiting in the queue, the server does not create a duplicate queue item.
- For a matching waiting queue item, the newer request updates the stored queued settings in place, keeps the same queue request id, and keeps the same queue position.
- For a matching waiting queue item, the record keeps its original `createdAt`, source-surface provenance, and FIFO position while refreshing `updatedAt` and replacing the stored normalized request settings with the latest request.
- If a matching queue item is already running, the server still avoids creating a duplicate queue item, but it does not mutate the active run's settings mid-flight.
- The duplicate-request rule applies across both start-ingest and re-embed requests once they resolve to the same canonical embed target path.
- When a duplicate request is collapsed onto an existing queue item, the server returns success and reuses the existing queue request id instead of returning a duplicate-specific error.
- Queue-aware success responses expose `queued`, `requestId`, and `queuePosition`.
- `requestId` is the durable queue identifier for this story.
- `runId` remains the active ingest-run identifier once work has actually started.
- Queue-aware success responses do not expose a separate `deduped` field in this story.
- For an immediately started request, the success payload includes the queue request id, the active `runId`, and a non-waiting queue state.
- For a waiting request, the success payload includes `queued: true`, the queue request id, the current queue position, and no active `runId` yet.
- `queuePosition` counts only waiting requests; an already running item uses the non-waiting state instead of reporting itself as queue position `1`.
- Flow, command, and MCP re-embed callers that previously blocked until terminal completion still block until the queued request reaches a terminal outcome.
- Queue wait time is treated as part of the blocking contract for those callers rather than as a reason to return early.
- The preferred blocking path waits for real queue-item or ingest completion events rather than relying on a short fixed timeout as the normal control mechanism.
- A much longer safety timeout may still exist as a final guard, but it is not the normal success path for correctly queued work.
- The frontend ingest surfaces show when a repository is queued for re-embed and show its queue position in the repository list.
- Queued state and queue position are added to the shared repository-list payload used by the ingest repo-list surfaces, rather than mirrored into unrelated flow-facing status payloads just for parity.
- The shared repository-list schema version, REST `/ingest/roots` response, classic MCP `ListIngestedRepositories` response schema, and client normalization are updated together so queued rows can expose `requestId`, waiting-only `queuePosition`, and a `runId` that is absent until execution actually starts.
- If a brand-new repository is queued before its first ingest run starts, the repository list still shows a temporary queued row right away.
- Queued repository visibility is stable enough that a user can refresh or revisit the ingest page and still see that the request is waiting.
- While a run is already active, the ingest UI still allows queueable start-ingest and re-embed submissions instead of blocking them behind a global active-run disable state; controls may remain disabled only when they are blocked for a separate destructive or invalid-state reason.
- After a queueable submission is accepted, any later edits to the retained visible form fields affect only a later explicit submit; they do not silently mutate the already accepted queue item.
- Removing the active-run disable gate does not change existing lock-driven field behavior: if the embedding model is locked, the model selector remains read-only and submissions keep using that locked model identity.
- Existing single-flight ingest execution still applies at runtime: only one ingest or re-embed run is active at a time, even though multiple future requests may now be queued durably.
- The queue request id may use the MongoDB document id generated for that queue item.
- On startup, cleanup-blocked queue items are retried or resolved before the server starts any newer waiting item.
- REST queue-backend outages return HTTP `503 Service Unavailable` with `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE`; MCP, flow, and command surfaces preserve `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` as a structured retryable error instead of collapsing it into a generic invalid-request failure.
- This story does not require queued-but-not-started requests to be removable by the user once they are in the queue.
- Documentation and tests are updated to describe the durable queue contract, dedupe behavior, startup recovery, blocking caller behavior, and frontend queued-state visibility.

### Out Of Scope

- User-driven removal or cancellation of queued-but-not-started requests.
- Priority queues, non-FIFO ordering, or queue reordering controls.
- Multiple concurrent ingest workers processing more than one queued request at once.
- Replacing the existing internal file-chunking and embedding-dispatch optimizations planned elsewhere.
- Adding a degraded mode that still starts queueable requests when MongoDB is unavailable.
- Returning a separate `deduped` response field instead of the queue-oriented response contract defined here.
- Broad redesign of the ingest frontend beyond what is needed to show queued state and queue position.
- Adding a dedicated top-of-page queue card for queued re-embed work.
- Adding queue-position fields to unrelated non-repository read surfaces when they are not acting as the story's required source of truth.
- Exactly-once execution guarantees across crashes or restarts.

## Questions

- No Further Questions

## Decisions

1. Queue position should count only waiting requests.
   - The question being addressed: Should queue position count only waiting requests, or should it also count the request that is already running?
   - Why the question matters: The frontend and API both need one stable meaning for `queuePosition`, especially when one request is already running and another is next in line.
   - What the answer is: Count only waiting requests, so the first waiting job shows `queuePosition: 1`, and an already running job uses the non-waiting state without a queue position.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [planning/0000055-users-can-queue-ingest-and-re-embed-requests.md](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/planning/0000055-users-can-queue-ingest-and-re-embed-requests.md), [server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts), [server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts), and [server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts), plus external evidence from DeepWiki's BullMQ docs noting that user-facing queue position is application-level logic built on waiting-versus-active job lists. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It is clearer for users because `1` means “next in line,” and it matches the story's existing rule that immediately started work should return a non-waiting queue state instead of pretending it is still queued.
2. Newer settings should replace older settings for a matching waiting queue item.
   - The question being addressed: If the same repository is already queued with different settings, should the first request stay or should the newer one replace it?
   - Why the question matters: Dedupe by canonical embed path is already part of the story, but we still need one clear rule for conflicting provider or model choices on that same path.
   - What the answer is: If the matching queue item is still waiting, the newer request replaces the stored queued settings in place while keeping the same `requestId` and queue position. If the matching item is already running, the server still avoids creating a second queue item, but it does not mutate the active run's settings mid-flight.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts), [server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts), [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts), and [server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts), plus external evidence from DeepWiki's BullMQ docs showing queues often dedupe on one job identity while the product still chooses how to treat later duplicates. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It lets users correct a queued request without losing its place in line, while still avoiding the higher-risk behavior of trying to rewrite an ingest that has already started.
3. Finished queue-item deletion should retry automatically and surface an error.
   - The question being addressed: If removing the finished queue item fails, should the server keep retrying automatically or stop and wait for a manual fix?
   - Why the question matters: The story already says the next queued run must not start before the finished queue record is removed, so we still need to decide whether recovery is automatic or purely manual and how visible that failure is to users.
   - What the answer is: Retry deletion automatically with backoff, keep the queue stalled until that delete succeeds, log an error, and show an error state in the frontend while the queue is blocked.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [planning/0000055-users-can-queue-ingest-and-re-embed-requests.md](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/planning/0000055-users-can-queue-ingest-and-re-embed-requests.md) and [server/src/ingest/lock.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/lock.ts), plus external evidence from official MongoDB retryable-write guidance showing MongoDB is designed to recover from transient write failures with bounded retries and DeepWiki's BullMQ queue docs, which treat cleanup and stalled-job recovery as automatic retry territory rather than purely manual intervention. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It preserves FIFO correctness, self-heals common transient failures, and still gives both operators and users a clear signal that the queue is blocked on cleanup rather than silently appearing idle.
4. Queue responses should keep both `requestId` and `runId`.
   - The question being addressed: Should queue responses keep `runId`, or should `requestId` be the only ID?
   - Why the question matters: Today the ingest routes, polling, and tests all work through `runId`, but this story adds a durable `requestId` for queued work.
   - What the answer is: Keep both. `requestId` is the durable queue identifier, and `runId` remains the active ingest identifier once work has actually started. A waiting item can therefore return `requestId` with no active `runId` yet.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts), [server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts), [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts), [client/src/components/ingest/IngestForm.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/components/ingest/IngestForm.tsx), and the current ingest step definitions under [server/src/test/steps](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/test/steps), plus external evidence from BullMQ docs on unique job IDs and DeepWiki queue guidance around waiting vs active job state. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It preserves existing active-run tooling while still giving queued work its own durable identifier.
5. Queued re-embed state should live in the repository list, not a new queue card.
   - The question being addressed: Should queued re-embed status show in the repository list only, or also in a top-of-page queue card?
   - Why the question matters: The story already says queued state must survive refresh, but we still need one clear primary UI surface so the frontend contract does not sprawl.
   - What the answer is: Make the repository list the required source of truth and keep a dedicated top-of-page queue card out of scope for this story.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [client/src/pages/IngestPage.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/pages/IngestPage.tsx), [client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts), [client/src/hooks/useIngestStatus.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/hooks/useIngestStatus.ts), and [client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx), plus external evidence from BullMQ docs and DeepWiki guidance distinguishing waiting jobs from active jobs and describing queue position as application-level state derived from waiting jobs. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: The repository row already matches the re-embed target, survives refresh naturally, and avoids expanding the UI scope with a second special-purpose queue surface.
6. Flows, commands, and MCP should wait through the queue by default.
   - The question being addressed: Should flows, commands, and MCP wait through the whole queue, or fail after a short timeout?
   - Why the question matters: The story says these callers should still block until completion, but the current re-embed service only waits about 90 seconds before giving up.
   - What the answer is: These callers should wait through the whole queue and the actual ingest run. The preferred implementation is event-driven waiting for queue-item and ingest completion, with only a much longer safety timeout as a final guard rather than as the normal control path.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts), [server/src/ingest/reingestExecution.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestExecution.ts), [server/src/flows/service.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/flows/service.ts), and [server/src/mcp/server.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mcp/server.ts), which show the current blocking contract and its short wait budget; external evidence from DeepWiki's BullMQ documentation on `waitUntilFinished`-style blocking and the distinction between queue delay and actual execution; Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today; and web search evidence from official BullMQ docs describing waiting vs active states and how active work continues until it completes.
   - Why it is the best answer: Queue delay becomes normal behavior in this story, so callers should not fail just because they had to wait their turn. Event-driven waiting also matches the real completion model better than treating a short timeout as the primary control mechanism.
7. A brand-new queued repository should appear in the repository list right away.
   - The question being addressed: If a brand-new repository is queued, should the repository list show a temporary row right away, or wait until the run starts?
   - Why the question matters: The repository list is now the required queued-state surface, but a brand-new start-ingest request may not have an existing repository row yet.
   - What the answer is: Show a temporary row right away so queued start-ingest work is visible in the same repository-list surface as queued re-embed work.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [client/src/pages/IngestPage.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/pages/IngestPage.tsx), [client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts), [client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx), and [server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts), plus external evidence from DeepWiki's BullMQ guidance on exposing waiting items before they become active. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It keeps the repository list as the single source of truth, avoids inventing a second queued-state surface, and gives immediate visible confirmation that a brand-new ingest request was accepted.
8. Startup recovery should clear cleanup-blocked items before newer waiting work.
   - The question being addressed: When the server restarts, should cleanup-blocked items be fixed before any new queued work starts?
   - Why the question matters: The story already says delete failures block the queue, but startup recovery still needs one clear rule about whether blocked cleanup or fresh queued work goes first after a restart.
   - What the answer is: Retry or resolve cleanup-blocked items first, and only start the next waiting request after that blocked state is cleared.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [planning/0000055-users-can-queue-ingest-and-re-embed-requests.md](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/planning/0000055-users-can-queue-ingest-and-re-embed-requests.md), [server/src/ingest/lock.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/lock.ts), and [server/src/index.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/index.ts), plus external evidence from DeepWiki's BullMQ recovery guidance on stalled and leftover jobs. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It preserves FIFO behavior and prevents the queue from silently advancing past a record that was explicitly meant to stall progress.
9. Mongo outages should return a clear retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` error.
   - The question being addressed: If Mongo is unavailable, should queue requests return a clear retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` error?
   - Why the question matters: The story already says these requests must be rejected when Mongo is down, but it still does not pin down a client-visible error contract that tells users and agents nothing started.
   - What the answer is: Return a clear retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` error, preferably as a temporary-service response rather than a generic server failure.
   - Where the answer came from: User decision in this planning session, supported by repo evidence from [server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts), [server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts), [server/src/ingest/requestContracts.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/requestContracts.ts), and [server/src/mongo/connection.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mongo/connection.ts), plus external evidence from RFC 9110 guidance on `503 Service Unavailable` and retryability and DeepWiki queue guidance on backend-unavailable retries. Context7 could not be queried because the workspace quota is exhausted today.
   - Why it is the best answer: It clearly tells callers the queue backend is temporarily unavailable, nothing ran, and retrying later is reasonable.

10. Use exactly `waiting`, `running`, and `cleanup-blocked` as the persisted queue-state values.

- The question being addressed: What exact persisted queue-state values should the Mongo queue document support so startup recovery can deterministically distinguish a normal waiting item, an abandoned previously-running item that should be retried, and a cleanup-blocked finished item that must be deleted before newer work can start?
- Why the question matters: Startup recovery and delete-before-next ordering both depend on one unambiguous persisted state model. If the queue-state model is too vague, restart logic becomes fragile; if it is too large, we add unnecessary complexity to a story that only needs durable FIFO orchestration.
- What the answer is: Persist only `waiting`, `running`, and `cleanup-blocked`. Do not add a separate persisted `abandoned` state. On startup, any leftover `running` record is the abandoned previously-active item and should be retried before newer waiting work. Terminal runs that clean up successfully should have their queue record deleted instead of persisting extra finished states.
- Where the answer came from: Direct repo evidence from [server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts), [server/src/ingest/lock.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/lock.ts), [server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts), plus DeepWiki `taskforcesh/bullmq` restart-recovery guidance on waiting, active, and stalled work.
- Why it is the best answer: It is the smallest durable state model that cleanly distinguishes all three story cases without duplicating ingest run phases or introducing finished states the queue immediately deletes anyway.

11. Expose queued state and queue position on the shared repository-list payload, not on every other status surface.

- The question being addressed: Which exact read surfaces need to expose queued state and queue position for this story: only the REST ingest-roots response used by the ingest page, or also MCP/listing surfaces and any flow-facing status payloads that currently describe ingest progress?
- Why the question matters: The story needs stable queued visibility, but adding `queuePosition` everywhere would expand scope and create extra contract churn. We need the smallest surface area that still keeps the required ingest visibility accurate.
- What the answer is: Add queued state and queue position to the shared repository-list payload that powers the ingest repository list and its existing mirrors, so `/ingest/roots` and the repo-list listing surfaces stay aligned. Do not add queue-position fields to unrelated flow-facing or generic status payloads just for parity. Queue-aware initiation responses still return `queued`, `requestId`, and `queuePosition`, but those are write contracts rather than extra read surfaces.
- Where the answer came from: Direct repo evidence from [server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts), [server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts), [client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts), and [client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx), plus DeepWiki `taskforcesh/bullmq` documentation that treats queue position as application-level waiting-job state rather than a universal surface field.
- Why it is the best answer: It satisfies the story's required source of truth, preserves existing shared payload patterns, and avoids spreading queue-position concerns into surfaces that do not need them.

12. Keep creation and provenance fields stable and refresh only `updatedAt` plus the normalized queued settings payload.

- The question being addressed: When a later duplicate request updates an existing waiting queue item in place, which audit fields must remain stable versus refresh, specifically `createdAt`, any new `updatedAt`, source-surface metadata, and the stored provider/model/embed settings payload?
- Why the question matters: The story promises that a waiting duplicate keeps its identity and queue position, but it still needs one precise rule for which fields preserve queue provenance and which fields reflect the latest effective request.
- What the answer is: Keep the durable request identity, queue order, `createdAt`, canonical target path, and original source-surface provenance stable. Refresh `updatedAt`, and replace the stored normalized provider/model/embed settings payload with the newest request instead of deep-merging it. Log the updating surface when the replacement happens; do not add extra audit-history fields in this story.
- Where the answer came from: Direct repo evidence from [server/src/mongo/repo.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mongo/repo.ts), [server/src/mongo/connection.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mongo/connection.ts), plus Context7 Mongoose timestamp documentation describing stable `createdAt` and refreshed `updatedAt` behavior on update operations.
- Why it is the best answer: It preserves FIFO identity and provenance, gives the queue one clear effective settings payload to run later, and keeps audit behavior simple without inventing extra history tables or merge rules.

13. Pin down `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` now as a transport-specific wrapper around one shared retryable error meaning.

- The question being addressed: Should the retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` contract be pinned down per transport now as `503 Service Unavailable` for REST plus equivalent retryable structured errors for MCP, flows, and commands, or is a different cross-surface error mapping intended?
- Why the question matters: If queue persistence is down, callers need to know nothing started and retrying later is sensible. Leaving the mapping vague would let different surfaces drift into generic failures, which breaks automation and user expectations.
- What the answer is: Yes. Pin it down now. REST should return HTTP `503 Service Unavailable` with `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE`, and may include `Retry-After` when the server has a meaningful delay to suggest. MCP, flows, and commands should preserve the same machine-readable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` code inside their transport-appropriate structured error envelopes with `retryable: true`, rather than collapsing the condition into generic invalid-request or opaque server-failure text.
- Where the answer came from: Direct repo evidence from [server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts), [server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts), [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts), and [server/src/mcp/server.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mcp/server.ts), plus RFC 9110 `503 Service Unavailable` guidance and the repo's existing structured non-HTTP error patterns.
- Why it is the best answer: It gives every caller one stable retryable queue-outage contract, matches normal HTTP semantics on REST, and avoids introducing transport-specific domain codes that would make clients harder to keep in sync.

## Log Or Proof Markers

- Queue write-contract proof marker: `QUEUE_REQUEST_ACCEPTED_WITH_REQUEST_ID`
  - Expected outcome: A queued request response proves the request/run split by exposing `requestId`, omitting `runId`, and returning a waiting-only `queuePosition`.
- Queue dedupe proof marker: `QUEUE_WAITING_DUPLICATE_REUSED`
  - Expected outcome: A second request for the same canonical target while the first item is still waiting returns success with the same `requestId` and queue position instead of creating another queue item.
- Startup recovery proof marker: `QUEUE_STARTUP_RECOVERY_RESUMED_IN_ORDER`
  - Expected outcome: After a restart, any cleanup-blocked item is resolved before the next waiting item starts, and the oldest remaining waiting item resumes without relying on manual intervention or arbitrary fixed delays.

## Runtime And Repo Prerequisites

- Existing runtime entrypoints already cover this story and should remain the active runtime path:
  - [server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestStart.ts)
  - [server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestReembed.ts)
  - [server/src/routes/ingestCancel.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestCancel.ts)
  - [server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts)
- Existing blocking re-embed callers already route through the current server implementation and therefore must be updated as part of this story rather than left on legacy behavior:
  - [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts)
  - [server/src/ingest/reingestExecution.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestExecution.ts)
  - [server/src/mcp/server.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mcp/server.ts)
  - [server/src/agents/commandsRunner.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/agents/commandsRunner.ts)
- Mongo connectivity already exists through [server/src/mongo/connection.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mongo/connection.ts); this story should reuse that connection path and fail queueable requests clearly when it is unavailable rather than inventing a fallback execution mode.
- Server startup already connects Mongo before the process begins listening in [server/src/index.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/index.ts), and `/health` already exposes `mongoConnected`. Queue recovery should hook into that existing startup path after Mongo connection succeeds and before the runtime is treated as ready, rather than inventing a second readiness endpoint just for this story.
- Existing request normalization already lives in [server/src/ingest/requestContracts.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/requestContracts.ts), so queue dedupe must happen after canonical path and embedding-selection resolution rather than from raw route parameters.
- Existing container and wrapper paths already cover this story in both the main and e2e stacks through [docker-compose.yml](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/docker-compose.yml), [docker-compose.e2e.yml](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/docker-compose.e2e.yml), [server/Dockerfile](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/Dockerfile), [client/Dockerfile](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/Dockerfile), [server/entrypoint.sh](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/entrypoint.sh), and [.dockerignore](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/.dockerignore). Those paths already copy application source into images, publish the current ports, and provision Mongo plus Chroma, so this story should stay inside the existing server process and should not add a new service, bind-mounted app source, port, volume, or queue-specific env knob unless later evidence proves the current runtime cannot own the queue safely.
- [server/src/ingest/config.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/config.ts) and [server/src/ingest/embeddingDispatcher.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/embeddingDispatcher.ts) already use `CODEINFO_INGEST_MAX_QUEUE_SIZE` for the per-run embedding dispatcher queue. This story must not silently reuse that existing env var for whole-request admission, dedupe, or cleanup backoff because it already means something narrower in the runtime today.
- Queue behavior must run on the default server path rather than behind a story-specific launcher or flag. The standard boot path in [server/src/index.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/index.ts), the normal REST routers, the shared repo-list readers, and the existing MCP/flow/command entry points are the required reachability path for this story.
- No new frontend page, new server listener, additional repository, or separate worker service is required by current repository evidence for this story.

## Message Contracts And Storage Shapes

- Current route contracts are still single-flight:
  - `POST /ingest/start` returns `202 { runId }` or `429 { status:'error', code:'BUSY' }`.
  - `POST /ingest/reembed/:root` returns `202 { runId }` or `429 { status:'error', code:'BUSY' }`.
  - `GET /ingest/status/:runId` remains the active per-run progress surface.
- This story should replace the write-side success contract for queueable start and re-embed requests with a queue-aware shape that is explicit enough for later tasking:
  - immediately started success: `queued: false`, `requestId`, `runId`, and no waiting queue position;
  - waiting success: `queued: true`, `requestId`, `queuePosition`, and no active `runId` yet;
  - duplicate waiting updates reuse the same `requestId` and queue position instead of returning a duplicate-only error.
- Queue-aware REST failure responses should keep the repo's current error-envelope style rather than inventing a second format. For queue persistence outages, the plan should assume `503` with a JSON body shaped like the existing ingest route failures: `{ status: 'error', code: 'QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE', retryable: true, message: string }`, plus an optional HTTP `Retry-After` header when the server has a meaningful retry delay to suggest.
- The durable queue document should stay intentionally small and explicit. At minimum it must carry:
  - one durable request identity, preferably the Mongo `_id`;
  - canonical target path and operation type;
  - persisted queue state `waiting | running | cleanup-blocked`;
  - created and updated timestamps;
  - the normalized request settings that will later drive the run;
  - enough provenance to explain where the request came from when troubleshooting or proving updates.
- Queue-document ownership should stay explicit in the plan. The shared admission helper is the only write path that creates or updates waiting queue items, the queue pump and startup-recovery paths are the readers that promote waiting items into active execution, the shared repo-list readers may read queue state for visibility but do not mutate it, and the terminal cleanup path is the only code allowed to delete queue documents after completion, error, or cancellation.
- The queue collection should follow the repo's existing Mongoose timestamp pattern (`timestamps: true`) and use indexed selectors for duplicate handling and FIFO reads. Prefer an indexed `findOneAndUpdate(..., { returnDocument: 'after' })` or equivalent single-document operation for duplicate waiting-item reuse, and do not rely on unindexed upsert behavior for atomicity. The canonical target-path selector and queue-order selector must therefore be backed by concrete indexes before later tasking relies on them.
- Canonical target-path normalization should reuse the repo's existing path-normalization surfaces instead of inventing a story-specific third path rule. Start-ingest paths already flow through [server/src/ingest/pathMap.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/pathMap.ts) when the repo list projects container paths, while selector-based re-embed callers already normalize container paths in [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts) and [server/src/mcpCommon/repositorySelector.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mcpCommon/repositorySelector.ts). Later implementation should therefore centralize on one shared canonical container-path helper that produces the same queue key for start-ingest, re-embed, repo-list readers, and MCP/command selector resolution.
- Queue-position and recovery selectors must be concretely bounded now, not left to later tasking guesswork. Waiting-only `queuePosition` should come from indexed queue-document selectors, for example counting older `waiting` documents by `createdAt`, and startup recovery should fetch the oldest `cleanup-blocked`, `running`, or `waiting` candidates with ordered indexed reads such as `findOne(...).sort(...)` rather than loading the whole queue just to decide what starts next. Reading the queue collection to project user-visible queue rows is acceptable because it is one document per queued request rather than per file or chunk, but write-side dedupe, queue-position, and recovery decisions must not degrade into unbounded scans by raw path text.
- The shared repository-list contract is currently version `0000038-status-phase-v1`, and its common types are still run-centric: [common/src/lmstudio.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/common/src/lmstudio.ts) exposes only `status` plus `phase`, [server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts) models rows around one `id`, and [client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/hooks/useIngestRoots.ts) expects a `runId` string on each normalized row. Because a waiting queue item has a durable `requestId` before any `runId` exists, this story must extend the shared repo-list contract in one place instead of overloading `runId`; if the queued row shape needs a new identifier or nullable `runId`, bump the shared schema version and update server plus client consumers together.
- The queue-aware repo-list contract should be stated concretely so later tasking does not guess. A queued row needs an explicit `requestId`, an optional `runId` that stays `null` or absent until execution actually starts, and a waiting-only `queuePosition` that is a positive integer when `queued: true` and absent otherwise. Because the classic MCP `ListIngestedRepositories` schema in [server/src/mcp/server.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/mcp/server.ts) currently hard-codes the older run-centric shape, the schema version bump must update that MCP output schema and the shared client/common types in the same story.
- The repository-list read contract is the required queued-state source of truth for users. Add queued state and waiting-only queue position to the shared repo-list payload that already feeds the ingest page and its mirrors, but do not mirror queue-position fields into unrelated generic status payloads purely for symmetry.
- Repo-list readers should follow the same live-overlay precedence pattern the repo already uses for active runs. When the same canonical target has both persisted terminal root metadata and a live queue document, the queue document owns live fields such as `requestId`, `runId`, `status`, and `queuePosition`, while persisted root metadata may still supply stable descriptive fields like name, description, counts, and `lastIngestAt` only when doing so does not contradict the live queue state.
- Queue-backed repository rows, including brand-new roots that have never been ingested, should be synthesized in the shared server list builders ([server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts) and [server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts)) before the React hook normalizes them, so REST, MCP, and UI mirrors all consume the same canonical queued view.
- The blocking re-embed surfaces should keep their existing terminal-completion promise, but their internal wait contract must change from today's short poll-timeout bias to a queue-aware wait that treats queue delay as normal behavior.

## Test Harnesses

- Existing server unit coverage already touches the main seams this story will change and should remain the primary proof surface:
  - [server/src/test/unit/ingest-start.test.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/test/unit/ingest-start.test.ts)
  - [server/src/test/unit/ingest-status.test.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/test/unit/ingest-status.test.ts)
  - [server/src/test/unit/ingest-dispatcher.test.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/test/unit/ingest-dispatcher.test.ts)
- Existing integration and cucumber seams already exercise ingest start, re-embed, roots, and delta behavior and should be extended instead of creating a brand-new harness:
  - [server/src/test/integration/ingest-reembed.test.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/test/integration/ingest-reembed.test.ts)

  - [server/src/test/features/ingest-status.feature](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/test/features/ingest-status.feature)

Later tasking should reuse those Testcontainers-backed seams, including `@mongo` coverage where queue persistence matters, rather than inventing bespoke local setup.
- Existing browser proof already exists through [e2e/ingest.spec.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/e2e/ingest.spec.ts) and the ingest-page React tests under `client/src/test/`; later tasking should extend those rather than inventing a second UI harness.
- Manual browser validation is already realistic without extra tooling because [playwright.config.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/playwright.config.ts) captures screenshots by default and the main compose stack already exposes a Playwright MCP service in [docker-compose.yml](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/docker-compose.yml). Final proof can therefore require both repo e2e coverage and manual Playwright MCP validation for queued UI states without first creating another browser harness.
- Startup-recovery, cleanup-blocked, and “next item has not started yet” proofs must use deterministic observable boundaries instead of arbitrary fixed delays. Later tasking should prove those paths through explicit state inspection, restart boundaries, or named proof markers while keeping Mongo-backed test state isolated per run.
- Stateful UI proof should separately cover “retained locally” versus “submitted again”: one proof path should show that a successful queued submit leaves the visible form values available for editing, and another should show that the already accepted queue item changes only after a second explicit submit for the same canonical target.
- Final proof for this story should explicitly cover:
  - FIFO waiting behavior and immediate-start behavior;
  - duplicate collapse for waiting items and non-mutation for running items;
  - startup retry of leftover `running` work and cleanup-blocked-before-next ordering;
  - queue-aware blocking behavior for re-embed callers;
  - repository-list queued visibility, including a brand-new queued root row.

## Edge Cases And Failure Modes

- The current repo still has hard single-flight `BUSY` checks in the start and re-embed routes plus a `90_000 ms` polling wait in [server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/ingest/reingestService.ts). Later tasking must replace those consistently so the product does not end up half-queued and half-single-flight.
- The current client still disables start, re-embed, and remove actions whenever any run is active because [client/src/pages/IngestPage.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/pages/IngestPage.tsx) passes `disabled={isRunActive}` into both the form and the roots table, and [client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/client/src/components/ingest/RootsTable.tsx) derives row/button disablement from that shared `busy` state. Later tasking must remove only the gating that conflicts with queued acceptance while still preserving genuinely destructive protections.
- Queue dedupe must happen on the canonical target path after normalization, not on raw request text or route params, otherwise start-ingest and re-embed requests for the same repository can still diverge.
- The queue state visible to users must remain waiting-only for `queuePosition`; already-running work should not pretend to be queue position `1`.
- The existing `CODEINFO_INGEST_MAX_QUEUE_SIZE` setting already bounds the embedding dispatcher's internal work queue, so using it for request-level queue admission or delete-retry behavior would couple two different scales incorrectly. Request-queue sizing and cleanup retry behavior should stay code-defined in this story unless fresh repo evidence proves a separate operator-facing control is required.
- Because the shared repo-list types currently assume a run-centric row shape, waiting queue items cannot be represented safely by pretending `requestId === runId`. The plan must keep those identifiers distinct all the way through the shared server and client contract.
- Queue dedupe, startup replay, and queue-position lookups must stay index-backed and bounded as repository counts grow. The plan should avoid any later design that requires scanning the full queue collection by raw path text just to decide whether a request can be inserted or to compute the next waiting position.
- Because the UI may now keep visible form state while queue items already exist, the server must remain authoritative when stale or repeated client input arrives. A repeated submit for the same canonical target should flow through the queue's duplicate-update or running-item-reuse rules rather than relying on the client to prevent mixed state perfectly.
- Active-run cancellation must still flow through the same terminal cleanup ownership as completion and error. If a queued request has already started and its ingest run is cancelled, the owning queue document still needs terminal cleanup before the next waiting item may start; cancellation must not strand a `running` queue record indefinitely.
- Cleanup-blocked records must prevent the queue from advancing on both live runtime and startup recovery paths; otherwise FIFO ordering silently breaks under delete failures.
- Because the repo-list is the required queued-state source of truth, a brand-new queued root needs a synthesized row immediately. Waiting for the first active run to start would make accepted queued work look lost.
- Mongo outages must fail before new work starts. A partial \"queue unavailable but run anyway\" branch would violate the durable-queue contract and create restart behavior the plan explicitly excludes.

## Implementation Ideas

- Server queue-storage seam: add one MongoDB collection for queued ingest work, for example `ingest_queue_requests`, with the Mongo `_id` used as the external `requestId`. Define the document shape, `timestamps: true`, the `waiting | running | cleanup-blocked` state enum, and the smallest useful indexes for canonical-target duplicate lookup and FIFO waiting-order reads.
- Server queue-admission seam: add one shared `enqueueOrReuseIngestRequest(...)` helper that runs after canonical path and embedding-selection resolution, rejects immediately when Mongo is unavailable, reuses the existing waiting item for a duplicate target with an indexed single-document update, reuses the existing running item without mutating it, or inserts a brand-new waiting queue item.
- Server duplicate-update seam: when the admission helper updates an existing waiting item, keep `requestId`, `createdAt`, canonical target path, and source-surface provenance stable; refresh `updatedAt`; replace the normalized request payload instead of deep-merging it; and return the post-update document so later callers do not have to re-read the queue item just to know what now owns the slot.
- Server queue-pump seam: add one shared `pumpIngestQueue()` function that reads the oldest eligible queue item, starts work only when the existing in-memory ingest lock is idle, and creates the real ingest `runId` only at the point where the queued request actually begins execution.
- Server terminal-cleanup seam: keep the active queue document in Mongo while the run is executing, then delete it before advancing the queue. If deletion fails, move the queue item into the `cleanup-blocked` path, expose the blocked error state, and retry cleanup with backoff without starting newer work.
- Server startup-recovery seam: hook queue recovery into the existing boot path in [server/src/index.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/index.ts) after `connectMongo(...)` succeeds and before the server is treated as ready. Resolve any `cleanup-blocked` item first, then retry leftover `running` work, then resume the oldest remaining `waiting` item.
- REST write-contract seam: update the start-ingest and re-embed routes so they stop returning single-flight `BUSY` for queueable requests, emit the queue-aware success shape (`queued`, `requestId`, `runId`, `queuePosition`), and return the explicit `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` outage contract when Mongo-backed queue persistence cannot accept the request.
- Blocking-caller seam: update flows, commands, and MCP re-embed callers so they enqueue or reuse a durable queue item first, then wait for that queued request's terminal outcome using queue-aware completion events rather than today's short polling timeout as the normal control path.
- Shared repo-list contract seam: update the shared repository-list data contract, schema version, and classic MCP `ListIngestedRepositories` schema together so queued rows can carry `requestId`, nullable-or-absent `runId` before execution starts, and waiting-only `queuePosition` without overloading the old run-centric shape.
- Server repo-list reader seam: extend [server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/lmstudio/toolService.ts) and [server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts](/Users/danielstapleton/Documents/dev/codeinfo2/codeInfo2/server/src/routes/ingestRoots.ts) so they overlay waiting queue entries from Mongo alongside active run contexts and Chroma roots, including synthesized rows for brand-new queued roots that do not yet exist in the persisted repo list.
- Client queue-visibility seam: update the ingest-page client normalization and rendering so queued rows consume the shared server-side repo-list contract, show waiting-only queue position, and stop relying on a global active-run disable state for queueable start-ingest and re-embed submissions. Keep queued visibility sourced from the shared repo-list contract rather than a separate local queue cache, keep retained visible form state local-only after a successful submit, and preserve lock-driven read-only field behavior where it already exists.
- Backend proof seam: add or extend server-side proof so the queue-storage, admission, duplicate-update, queue-pump, terminal-cleanup, startup-recovery, and `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` paths are all independently provable through unit plus Testcontainers/Cucumber coverage rather than one bundled “queue works” test.
- Frontend and end-to-end proof seam: add or extend client and Playwright proof so queued rows, waiting-only `queuePosition`, brand-new queued roots, and queueable submission behavior while another run is active are all validated separately from the backend persistence and recovery paths.

# Tasks

### Task 1. Add Durable Queue Storage And Canonical Admission Reuse

- Repository Name: `Current Repository`
- Task Dependencies: `None`
- Task Status: `__done__`
- Git Commits:
  - `05e5cc6c` - `DEV-[55] - add durable queue admission model`

#### Overview

This task adds the durable Mongo-backed queue artifact and the one shared admission helper that owns canonical-target dedupe for queueable ingest work. It must keep the persisted queue model intentionally small, reuse existing path-normalization rules instead of inventing new ones, and make waiting-duplicate updates deterministic before any route or UI contract changes happen downstream.

#### Task Exit Criteria

- One Mongo collection exists for whole-request queue items, uses exactly `waiting | running | cleanup-blocked`, uses the Mongo `_id` as the durable `requestId`, and has explicit indexes for canonical-target duplicate lookup plus FIFO waiting-order reads.
- One shared admission helper can reject queueable work when Mongo is unavailable, reuse a matching waiting item in place, reuse a matching running item without mutating it, preserve `createdAt` plus source-surface provenance on waiting-item updates, and calculate waiting-only `queuePosition` from older indexed queue documents after canonical target normalization.

#### Documentation Locations

- https://mongoosejs.com/docs/timestamps.html . Use this so the new queue model follows the repository’s existing `timestamps: true` pattern and keeps `createdAt` stable while `updatedAt` refreshes on waiting-item updates.
- https://mongoosejs.com/docs/tutorials/findoneandupdate.html . Use this for the duplicate waiting-item reuse path so the task relies on one atomic indexed update rather than a read-then-write race.
- https://mongoosejs.com/docs/guide.html#indexes . Use this to define the canonical-target and FIFO selectors explicitly instead of relying on collection scans.

### Task 2. Add Queue Runtime Lifecycle, Cleanup Ownership, And Startup Recovery

- Repository Name: `Current Repository`
- Task Dependencies: `1`
- Task Status: `__done__`
- Git Commits:
  - `65b908b8` - `DEV-[55] - finish task 2 queue runtime validation`

#### Overview

This task makes the durable queue actually run inside the existing server process. It keeps single-flight ingest execution at runtime, promotes waiting items in FIFO order, stalls safely on cleanup-blocked records, routes cancellation through the same cleanup owner, and resumes leftover queue work during normal startup without adding a second service or a story-specific launcher.

#### Task Exit Criteria

- The queue pump promotes only the oldest eligible queue item into active execution, assigns the real ingest `runId` only when work actually starts, keeps at most one active run at a time, and never starts the next waiting item before terminal cleanup of the current queue record succeeds.
- Startup recovery in the default server boot path resolves `cleanup-blocked` first, retries leftover `running` work next, and then resumes the oldest remaining `waiting` item in FIFO order, while cancellation, completion, and error all flow through the same queue-document cleanup owner.

#### Documentation Locations

- https://mongoosejs.com/docs/api/query.html . Use this for ordered `findOne(...).sort(...)`, `countDocuments(...)`, and other query semantics that keep recovery and queue-position selectors bounded and index-friendly.

#### Subtasks

1. [x] Read the Story 55 Description, Acceptance Criteria covering FIFO execution, cleanup-before-next ordering, startup recovery, active-run cancellation, and single-flight runtime behavior, plus Decisions 1, 3, and 10, the `Runtime And Repo Prerequisites` section, and the `Edge Cases And Failure Modes` section. Then inspect `server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts`, `server/src/ingest/lock.ts`, `server/src/index.ts`, and `server/src/routes/ingestCancel.ts`. Purpose: understand which unchanged runtime files already own active-run lifecycle, cleanup, and default startup wiring.
2. [x] Inspect `server/src/test/unit/ingest-status.test.ts`, `server/src/test/unit/ingest-cancel.test.ts`, `server/src/test/unit/ingest-dispatcher.test.ts`, `server/src/test/integration/ingest-reembed.test.ts`, `server/src/test/features/ingest-start.feature`, `server/src/test/features/ingest-reembed.feature`, `server/src/test/features/ingest-status.feature`, `server/src/test/steps/ingest-manage.steps.ts`, `server/src/test/support/mongoContainer.ts`, and `server/src/test/support/chromaContainer.ts` before editing runtime code. Purpose: anchor the runtime changes to the existing deterministic unit, integration, and Testcontainers-backed proof harnesses while keeping the embedding dispatcher’s separate queue semantics visibly unchanged.
3. [x] Update `server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts` to select the oldest eligible queue document by indexed order and promote it from `waiting` to `running` only when the existing ingest lock is idle. Purpose: make FIFO queue pumping respect the repo’s current single-flight runtime rule.
4. [x] Update `server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts` so the real ingest `runId` is created only when work actually starts and remains associated with the owning queue request while the run is active. Purpose: keep the story’s `requestId` versus `runId` split honest inside the runtime owner.
5. [x] Update the completion and error cleanup path in `server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts` so the owning queue document is deleted before any newer waiting item can start. Purpose: preserve FIFO ordering and prevent the queue from advancing past unfinished cleanup.

Purpose: keep restart behavior deterministic and consistent with the story’s coarse persisted queue-state model.

#### Implementation notes

- Starts empty.
- Read the Task 2 runtime ownership files and confirmed `ingestJob.ts` already owns active-run lifecycle and cancellation cleanup, `lock.ts` is still just the single-flight guard, and `index.ts` does not yet have any startup queue recovery hook.
- Reviewed the named unit, integration, and cucumber proof seams before editing runtime code so Task 2 can extend the current status/cancel/reembed harnesses instead of inventing a second runtime test path.
- Added queue-runtime ownership in `ingestJob.ts` for FIFO pump/startup recovery, request-to-run tracking, delete-before-next cleanup, and cleanup-blocked retry scheduling, then wired default startup recovery through `server/src/index.ts`.
- Added `server/src/test/unit/ingest-queue-runtime.test.ts` and a dedicated `ingestJob.ts` queue-runtime test seam so the immediate-start, FIFO, runId timing, delete-before-next, cleanup-blocked, and bounded recovery-selector behaviors are directly provable without mutating ESM exports.
- Tightened queue advancement so `pumpIngestQueue()` also stalls while terminal queue deletion is still in flight, not only after a cleanup-blocked write failure, which made the delete-before-next boundary deterministic for both unit and integration proof.
- Added status and cancel proof coverage for cleanup-blocked visibility and cancel-to-cleanup ordering, then replaced the old reembed integration stub with startup-recovery and cleanup-boundary tests that assert on explicit active-run or event boundaries instead of sleeps.
- Added `@mongo` cucumber scenarios plus queue-seeding steps for startup recovery ordering and cleanup-blocked stall behavior, and logged `QUEUE_STARTUP_RECOVERY_RESUMED_IN_ORDER` from startup recovery so the higher-level proof has a concrete observable marker.
- Ran the Task 2 ESLint file list clean with zero warnings, and ran Prettier on the touched server/test files plus the `.feature` files using the Markdown parser because the repo’s plain `prettier --check` invocation cannot infer a parser for cucumber feature files on its own.
- Re-ran targeted server-unit wrappers for `ingest-status`, `ingest-cancel`, `ingest-dispatcher`, `ingest-queue-runtime`, and the reembed integration file while tightening the runtime cleanup ordering and the queue test seam; the targeted cucumber wrapper for the Task 2 feature files also passed clean.
- **BLOCKING ANSWER** Repository precedents point to explicit teardown plus injected timing seams, not longer sleeps. In this repo, `server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts` already keeps `queueCleanupRetryTimers` in one place and `__resetIngestJobsForTest()` clears them, `server/src/ingest/providers/openaiRetry.ts` plus `server/src/test/unit/openai-provider-retry.test.ts` prove retry behavior through injected timing seams instead of real waiting, and `server/src/test/integration/flows.run.loop.test.ts` plus `server/src/test/support/wsClient.ts` explicitly close long-lived runtime handles before the test process exits. External/library precedents line up with that: Node's `node:test` docs say completed tests can still leave extraneous async activity behind and that each test file runs in its own child process (`https://nodejs.org/download/release/v22.12.0/docs/api/test.html`), while Node's timers docs say `Timeout` handles are ref'ed by default and `timeout.unref()` allows the process to exit when no other work remains (`https://nodejs.org/download/release/v22.12.0/docs/api/timers.html`). DeepWiki's `nodejs/node` docs summary also points to explicit `clearTimeout`, mock timers, and `unref()` as the supported patterns for timer-based tests. Context7 lookup for Node.js docs was attempted during blocker research but the service quota was exhausted, so the blocking answer uses the official Node docs directly instead. Issue-resolution references from engineers in practice match the same fix shape: `https://stackoverflow.com/questions/47312280/why-node-js-doesnt-exit-after-promise-call` and `https://stackoverflow.com/questions/18050095/node-js-will-node-always-wait-for-settimeout-to-complete-before-exiting` both explain that ref'ed timers, not promises, keep Node alive, while `https://www.bennadel.com/blog/3301-calling-timeout-unref-with-settimeout-does-not-appear-to-be-a-best-practice-in-node-js.htm` is the useful caution that `unref()` is correct only for background timers whose callback is not required to keep the process alive. The local proof matches those references: `scheduleQueueCleanupRetry()` in `server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts` currently creates a real `setTimeout` without `unref()`, and a disposable check showed `time -p node -e "setTimeout(() => {}, 2_000)"` stayed alive for `real 2.02`, while `time -p node -e "const h = setTimeout(() => {}, 2_000); console.log('hasRef-before', h.hasRef()); h.unref(); console.log('hasRef-after', h.hasRef());"` exited in `real 0.01`. Chosen fix: call `handle.unref?.()` on the cleanup-retry timeout inside `scheduleQueueCleanupRetry()`, keep `__resetIngestJobsForTest()` clearing outstanding retry timers, and if a proof must observe the retry callback itself, drive that path with the existing injected test seam or Node mock timers rather than real time. This fits the current repo because the cleanup retry is detached self-healing background work, not the proof boundary itself, and it is the only new long-lived timer introduced by Task 2. Rejected alternatives: increasing wrapper timeouts or adding sleeps only hides open handles; `process.exit()` or disabling test isolation are anti-patterns; moving all queue-runtime ownership proofs out of `ingest-queue-runtime.test.ts` is broader than needed; and converting the whole file to mock timers is optional cleanup, not the minimum correct fix for the blocker.
- Resolved the full-wrapper stall by making cleanup retries detached background timers with `handle.unref?.()` and by treating queue finalization without a remaining `requestId` owner as a no-op instead of recursively re-pumping forever; this cleared the queue-runtime unit file without weakening the delete-before-next semantics.
- Re-ran `npx eslint server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts --max-warnings=0`, `npx prettier --check server/src/ingest/ingestJob.ts`, `npm run build:summary:server`, `npm run test:summary:server:unit`, and `npm run test:summary:server:cucumber`, and all passed clean with `agent_action: skip_log`.
- Update it during implementation with concise notes describing what was done, what issues were encountered, and what decisions were made.
- If a blocker is found during implementation, record the exact subtask or testing step, what was attempted, and what capability is missing.

### Task 3. Replace Queueable Transport Contracts For REST, MCP, Commands, And Flows

- Repository Name: `Current Repository`
- Task Dependencies: `1, 2`
- Task Status: `__done__`
- Git Commits:
  - `34b3a09b` - `DEV-[55] - Replace queueable transport contracts`
  - `d5e8dcfb` - `DEV-[55] - Advance task 3 automated proof`
  - `1d7d4ae2` - `DEV-[55] - Record task 3 targeted proof`
  - `dfe8f0c8` - `DEV-[55] - Rerun task 3 proof wrappers`
  - `0e91ba7a` - `DEV-[55] - reopen task 3 after manual proof`
  - `774ee321` - `DEV-[55] - Remap queued reembed roots`
  - `8bdba93f` - `DEV-[55] - Record reopened task 3 audit`
  - `0366f477` - `DEV-[55] - Record task 3 automated proof rerun`

#### Overview

This task replaces the old single-flight write contracts on queueable surfaces with queue-aware request contracts while keeping blocking re-embed callers synchronous from the user’s point of view. It owns the transport behavior for REST start/re-embed requests, queue-aware `requestId` versus `runId`, retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE`, and blocking callers that now wait through queue delay rather than treating it as an early timeout failure.

#### Task Exit Criteria

- `POST /ingest/start` and `POST /ingest/reembed/:root` stop using the queueable `BUSY` response path and instead return the Story 55 queue-aware success and failure contracts, including `queued`, `requestId`, waiting-only `queuePosition`, an optional `runId` only after execution starts, and retryable `QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` when Mongo-backed queue persistence is unavailable.
- Blocking re-embed callers in the service, MCP, command, and flow layers enqueue or reuse a durable queue item first, then wait for the queued request’s actual terminal outcome through queue-aware events or state transitions, with a long safety timeout only as a last-resort broken-state guard rather than the normal success path.

#### Documentation Locations

- https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Headers/Retry-After . Use this for the optional REST `Retry-After` header on `503 QUEUE_UNAVAILABLE` responses so the response stays within standard HTTP semantics.
- https://nodejs.org/api/events.html#eventsonceemitter-name-options . Use this to implement queue-aware event-driven waiting in the blocking re-embed service instead of relying on the current short poll loop as the normal control path.

#### Implementation notes

- Starts empty.
- Re-read the full Task 3 story guidance plus the route, blocking-service, adapter, and proof files named in the task; the current transport layer still returns `BUSY` and a short poll wait, while Tasks 1 and 2 already provide the durable request queue, queue request ids, and runtime queue pump this task now needs to adopt.
